Criticism

The National Medical and Pharmaceutical Association's Letter to the Five Yuan Presidents 153

The National Medical and Pharmaceutical Associations Joint Federation sent a letter to the Five Yuan Presidents yesterday, saying: "President, we have read in the newspaper that the Chinese Medical and Pharmaceutical Association has sent a letter to you regarding the establishment of the National Medical Museum. We believe that this is not out of animosity towards traditional medicine or regret for the National Medical Museum. This shows that the association is being fair and reasonable, and is considering the matter calmly and rationally. They must have thought it over carefully and spoken thoughtfully. However, there are still some things that are not entirely true. In science, there are so-called reasons and principles. The thinking itself is a series of interconnected and interdependent phenomena. This is why the world never has unreasoned and accidental novel phenomena, nor sudden new events. Everything that seems new at first glance is actually a transformation of the old. Western medicine often uses science and novelty as a rallying cry, like holding the emperor hostage to command the princes. They are already benefiting from this. But to say that traditional medicine is absolutely unscientific is not right. Did Western medicine not evolve from the theory of the four humors and three elements to what it is today? Why can't Chinese medicine evolve from the theory of the seven prescriptions and ten dosages to reach science? Moreover, everything in the universe is material for science. To say that science is not enough to regulate Chinese medicine is to belittle Chinese medicine and to increasingly deviate from the scope of science that they use as a rallying cry.

Western medicine often falsely accuses Chinese medicine of being superstitious nonsense. But is Chinese medicine really knowledge or nonsense? The theory of the five movements and six qi is close to knowledge. But Chinese medicine shops do not sell the five movements and six qi. Chinese medicine prescriptions are not full of the five movements and six qi. They are only used as an auxiliary for research. However, we are not forever unwilling to improve. This is the origin of the saying that Chinese medicine should be scientific. This is the origin of the proposal to establish a National Medical Museum. To bring Chinese medicine to the realm of science and to bring Chinese medicine to the path of physics and chemistry is what we earnestly hope for the National Medical Museum and what we are willing to work together with the National Medical Museum to achieve. As for differentiating drugs into cold, hot, warm, and neutral, and differentiating diseases into internal injuries and external feelings, this is not nonsense, but is accurate. This is how diseases can be treated quickly and effectively. Western medicine divides the muscles of the human body into voluntary muscles and involuntary muscles. Voluntary muscles can be controlled by the mind and can move. Involuntary muscles can move freely even during sleep. Their analysis is very precise and their differences are very obvious. But are those who claim to be new doctors and scientific doctors different from the living and the dead? Are the healthy different from those under anesthesia? If there is no difference, then so be it. If there is a difference, then the respiratory and circulatory systems of the dead body have stopped. The voluntary muscles and sensory organs have become ineffective when a person is anesthetized for surgery. So, are the phenomena obtained from anatomy and surgery the phenomena of a normal person? Therefore, the theory of qi transformation in Chinese medicine is sometimes superior to the experience that Western medicine obtains from the dead. Which school of thought is knowledge and which is nonsense? The truth is in people's hearts. There is no need to make pointless arguments. As for comparing diagnosis by color and sound to blind doctors, these are just the words of rude children and shrewish women. They are unbearably vulgar and irredeemably foolish. There is no point in refuting them.

The words of Yang Quan's Theory of Physics are ignorant of the essence of Chinese medicine. Rhubarb drains and angelica relieves pain. But they do not know that the same fullness should be treated with major qi-regulating decoction if it is in the upper body, qi-regulating stomach-harmonizing decoction if it is in the middle body, and honey-fried guide if it is in the lower body to unblock it. The same accumulation is treated differently. Divine leaven eliminates food accumulation, dragon bone eliminates wheat accumulation, hawthorn eliminates meat accumulation, and tangerine peel eliminates fish accumulation. The same pain is treated differently. Dahurian angelica treats orthodox headaches, asarum treats migraines, mulberry leaves and chrysanthemums treat feverish headaches, cinnamon twig treats arm pain, gentian treats wind pain, coridius treats 　pain, left golden pill treats left hypochondriac pain, qi-dispersing powder treats right hypochondriac pain, mulberry mistletoe treats waist pain, deer antler treats back 　pain, peony and licorice treat abdominal pain, and achyranthes and clematis treat leg and knee pain. Angelica is only a tonic for blood deficiency pain and should be avoided for qi stagnation, stomach pain, diarrhea, and abdominal pain. Chinese medicine doctors can prescribe medicine and see results instantly, like a shadow following a pole. Is this as simple as the examples given by Western medicine?

As for saying that a fever lasting for several days is warm evil, there is also careful differentiation and confirmation in this. This is not something that can be loosely called a deer and then called a horse. I would like to ask if Western medicine always calls a common cold or cough influenza? Chinese medicine also differentiates between many symptoms of insomnia, and never generally calls it liver qi. There are those who cannot sleep because the stomach is not harmonized, those who cannot sleep because of fatigue and vexation, those who cannot sleep after illness, those who cannot sleep when old, those who think too much, those who have phlegm obstructing internally, those who have a fever that is too high and are restless and cannot sleep, and those who have vomited 　and have wrongly sweated and cannot sleep. The causes of the disease are different, and the prescriptions are different. How can it be said that the treatment of the disease is always the same? Those who are hot should be cooled, and those who are cold should be warmed. Moreover, they have not yet invented specific drugs, and the so-called specific drugs also come from abroad and cannot fully suit the constitution of the Chinese people. Can this be compared on the same day? If they do not know the efficacy of the drugs, then how can they make such extreme and derogatory statements? They will collapse on their own and only show their deep animosity towards traditional medicine. The funding for the National Medical Museum is only one-twelfth of the previous Ministry of Health and one-eighth of the current Ministry of Health. They think that if the National Medical Museum does not proceed according to their designated methods, it is a waste. Their deep desire for the National Medical Museum to live or die reveals their microscopic vision and their inability to see the big picture. They also show their deep regret for the National Medical Museum. Moreover, these people imitate the superficial aspects of Western medicine and promote the sale of foreign drugs. The country spends a lot of money to run medical schools for decades and create so-called medical doctors. What have they invented? What have they improved? They only say what the foreigners say. They only invade when others invade. They do not admonish themselves with the poem of the field rat, but instead falsely criticize the words of flattery. They do not know that a gentleman forgives anger. A gentleman is like happiness, and his words and deeds are carefully considered. What is the use of their inflammatory rhetoric? Alas, my compatriots know that the young are easily forced. They have just escaped the poison of thousands of years of autocratic politics and are now being robbed by scientific medicine and pharmaceuticals. If traditional Chinese medicine has any shortcomings or inadequacies, then they should write on the prescription and ask the patient to seek another expert. Scientific Western medicine is not like this. If you enter the hospital, you will either get better or you will die. Those who can afford to leave the hospital halfway have many troubles, and those who cannot afford it cannot do so. Moreover, many deaths are not reported and are arbitrarily dissected. Is this not autocracy? The association is worried that you do not know the essence of new and old medicine. I dare to present a brief outline, although it is not enough to dispel your doubts, it can at least inform the public and correct the situation.

Free Talk

World Tidbits 154

— Sea Guest

▲ A famous dancer in the United States asked a cosmetic surgeon to perform surgery to improve her appearance. Who knew that after the surgery, she couldn't smile? So she filed a lawsuit in court demanding 5,000 pounds in compensation.

▲ Once at a grand banquet in a large hotel in London, the waiters found a complete set of dentures, upper and lower. Within twenty-four hours, someone came to claim it. This person was a police officer who had inadvertently dropped it on the table while dining.

▲ In Maryport, Cumberland, in northwestern England, a fifteen-month-old baby was attacked by a gander. It grabbed the baby's throat and dragged it toward a small creek. Fortunately, someone came to the rescue and the baby was unharmed.

▲ The British are a world-renowned smoking nation. However, the statistics for cigar consumption in the United States, relative to the population, are even higher than in Britain.

▲ According to a survey in August 1923, there were a total of 15 million cars in the world. The United States alone accounted for 12 million. In recent years, it has greatly increased.

▲ Lake Superior in the United States is the largest freshwater lake in the world, with an area of 31,000 square miles. It is unparalleled in the world.

A Tragic Report from Kang Jiyao 155

— Sun Choucheng

Mr. Zhu Ziqiao, Chairman of the North China Charity Federation, is enthusiastically running around for the Shaanxi disaster. He sacrificed his position as a member of the Supervisory Yuan to come to Shanghai to raise funds. He is willing to go to Shaanxi again to provide relief. All sectors of the city admired his sincerity and formed the Shanghai Emergency Relief Fund Committee for the Shaanxi Disaster. Since its establishment, it has achieved great results, demonstrating that everyone has a heart of compassion. Mr. Zhu set up a banquet at the Gongdelin Vegetarian Restaurant the night before he left Shanghai to publicly invite fellow villagers and members of the China Merchants Cigarette Association to report on the disaster situation and ask them to donate as much as they could. He also introduced Mr. Kang Jiyao, Chairman of the Shaanxi Provincial Relief Committee, to the guests, saying that Mr. Kang had served as the Director of the Shaanxi Finance Department and was respected for his morality and writing. Recently, he also gave up his political career to focus on charity. He is very knowledgeable in Buddhism. He came to Shanghai from Shaanxi yesterday. Recently, he personally went to the disaster area to investigate. The situation he saw was more accurate than what I saw when I was providing relief in Shaanxi two months ago. So I specially invited him to attend and report. Mr. Kang is tall and thin, wearing a woolen gown and a black waistcoat. He has beautiful whiskers and holds a Buddhist rosary. He is fifty-one years old and in good spirits. At first glance, he resembles Mr. Wen Lantong, a prominent figure in Shanghai's business community. That night, Mr. Wen happened to be hosting a banquet in the next room. A gentleman at the next table said that tonight is like a double package deal. How could two philanthropists be so similar? Mr. Kang stood up and gave a speech. First, he bowed to the guests and thanked them on behalf of all the disaster victims in Shaanxi. Then, he said that the reports on the Shaanxi disaster only covered two or three tenths of the actual situation. At first, when I received reports from the branch committees in various counties, I thought they were exaggerated and was skeptical. So I personally went to the disaster area to conduct an on-the-spot investigation. The situation I saw was very tragic. Looking out over the barren fields, there was nothing but corpses. Not only were there starving people everywhere, but also corpses that had been accumulating for more than a year were still exposed, and no one was cleaning them up. To give you an example, there are a hundred families in Xinglin Town and only thirty households in Bawang Village. In one case, there were more than fifty corpses hidden in the house. In the other case, there were more than twenty corpses that had not been buried. In Wulin County, there were even more than thirteen thousand corpses exposed in the wilderness, and no one was taking care of them. I recall that there was also a major disaster in Shaanxi during the reign of Emperor Guangxu in the twenty-sixth year of Guangxu. The Qing court allocated a large sum of money to provide relief. But the disaster at that time was not as severe as the one in recent years, and the duration was not as long as this time. Now, when I go to the countryside to investigate the disaster, there is no one for dozens of miles. You don't need to use your eyes or ears, you just need to use your nose. Because when your nose smells foul odors, you know that the area is full of corpses and the disaster is severe. I hope that the gentlemen present will donate as much as they can. Those who cannot afford to donate money can spread the word and encourage others to donate. The Buddha said that there are four ways to give, but the merit is the same. Donating money is giving wealth. Encouraging others to donate is giving the Dharma. Comforting people who are afraid is giving fearlessness. Having a good thought when you cannot help is giving with your heart. Then, Mr. Cha Liangzhao, who had been bound and held captive by bandits for eighty-one days because of his relief efforts, reported on what he had witnessed in Shaanxi. He said that the severity of the Shaanxi disaster was too great to enumerate. I will present one or two things to give you a general idea. Wugong County used to be very prosperous. Last year, because the horse was sick, I wanted to buy two eggs as medicine, but I searched for dozens of miles and couldn't find any. Because the corpses had not been buried and the starving people were on their way, all the tree bark and grass roots had been eaten. There were no chickens or dogs left. How could there be chicken eggs? From this, you can imagine the tragic situation. There are other things, but I am afraid that after I describe them, you will not be able to eat. Therefore, I will not go into detail. Everyone was deeply saddened and willing to donate as much as they could. They also asked Mr. Zhu and Mr. Cha to continue providing relief in Shaanxi. The banquet ended at 9:00 PM.

Wind and Rain Pavilion of Jian Lake 156

— Xia Fei

Qiu Jin of Shaoxing competed for greatness in the autumn. She dedicated herself to the revolution and sacrificed her life for righteousness. Her heroic spirit and righteous deeds shine brightly through the ages. To commemorate this martyr, the Shaoxing County government has specially established halls for Cheng Zhang, Xi Lin, and Qiu Jin in Zhongshan Park, displaying the portraits and various mementos of the martyrs. Furthermore, a Wind and Rain Pavilion was built on the summit of Fu Mountain to commemorate Qiu Jin's line, "Autumn wind and rain are devastating," which she uttered when facing imminent danger. Additionally, a monument over ten feet tall was erected at Xuan Ting Kou, the place where Qiu Jin faced her execution. It was constructed purely of cement and aggregate, with the six large characters "Monument to Female Knight Qiu" inscribed on the upper layer of the front. Below, a bronze plaque bears the four characters "Heroine Among Women," a posthumous tribute by President Sun. After diligent construction, it will soon be completed, and a dedication ceremony will be held.

On Mr. Wang Xuequan's Affairs 157

— Xie Liwu

The gentleman's surname is Wang, given name Dingsheng, courtesy name Xuequan. His family has lived in Xian Village, She County, Anhui, for generations. Mr. Wang was born after his father, Mr. Xu Zhi, had passed away. He relied on his mother, Madam Xu, for upbringing and education. Mr. Wang was extraordinarily intelligent and mature beyond his years. At a young age, he studied the classics in Ru Zui Township. Later, he went to Heji Pawnshop in Changle Town, Haimen, and was soon promoted to treasurer. He then took on additional responsibilities. Mr. Jin, who was in charge of the pawnshop, resided in Shanghai and rarely visited throughout the year. Whether matters were significant or trivial, internal or external, he relied solely on Mr. Wang. Those who bear responsibility inevitably face complaints. Moreover, within the residency, petty people were in power, and the advancement or retreat of servants depended on their whims. They ostracized those who differed from them. Mr. Wang once upheld justice and wrote a letter to the resident, eloquent and forceful, filled with truth and righteousness, leaving no room for suppression. However, this further provoked the anger of the petty people. Slander and destruction intensified, leading to Mr. Wang's demotion to treasurer of Baochang Pawnshop in Bird Town. Mr. Wang read the resident's letter and smiled without anger. He replied with sincere gratitude, only pleading to resign due to his mother's old age and frequent illness. That winter, Mr. Wang returned home promptly to care for his mother. He also enclosed a small garden, planting flowers and stacking stones. Although lacking the grandeur of pavilions and towers, the undulating mountains brought greenery through the gate, sufficient to bring joy. Mr. Wang planned to retire and live in seclusion, reading and painting, fulfilling his desire for a small retreat. However, Mr. Liu Chengru of Nanxun, admired Mr. Wang's virtue and eagerly sought to recruit him. He entrusted someone to convey his intentions. Mr. Wang then went with Mr. Shen Lükui. Before they could even settle down, they felt like they had known each other for a long time. Mr. Liu also entrusted him with the affairs of Youxi Estate. The local people were cunning and often resisted paying rent. Mr. Wang forcefully rectified the situation, eliminating the accumulated abuses. All his plans were organized and methodical, greatly improving the collection of rent. Mr. Liu appreciated his ability even more and relied on him deeply. Last autumn, when Mr. Wang was at home, he suffered from a carbuncle on his face, which became dangerously severe. Acquaintances were worried about him. Fortunately, due to the efficacy of medicine, he recovered. Mr. Wang was secretly delighted and happily returned east. Who knew that disaster would strike unexpectedly, taking his life in a foreign land? Previously, troops stationed in Changzhou had infiltrated the surrounding villages. On the night of the fourth day of the twelfth month, a band of bandits suddenly arrived at the estate, plundering at will. Mr. Wang was loyal to his duty and unwilling to easily reveal the location of the hidden gold to the bandits, leading to their rage. He suffered a gunshot wound, hitting a vital spot, and could not be saved. At Shen hour on the seventh day of the twelfth month, he died in Wujin Hospital. Alas, how painful! Mr. Wang was intelligent and studious, excelling in writing, especially in official documents. When he was working at Changle, Mr. Zhang Jian, the Duke of Nantong, was developing transportation. He planned to demolish the Heji Pawnshop to clear the navigation route. Mr. Wang wrote a letter, arguing forcefully and unyielding, hitting the essential points, and ultimately stopping the demolition plan. Mr. Wang was amiable and approachable, especially chivalrous and righteous. Now, he has suffered this unusual misfortune. Oh, vast heavens, what will you say to this? I have known Mr. Wang for a long time and know his character in detail. Therefore, I write this biography, not only to record his admirable deeds but also to express my sorrow. (No remuneration accepted.)

Gleanings from the Fudan Female Students' Get-Together 158

— Fang

The female dormitory of Fudan University in Jiangwan is renowned as the "Eastern Palace" of the sea. The palace mistresses, however, do not acknowledge this themselves. Recently, they organized a female student association to promote virtue and learning. The other evening, they held a get-together in the dining hall. The scene was filled with the glittering of hairpins and the swaying of tresses, reaching the height of splendor. The curtain rose with Ms. Liang Peishu as chairwoman and Ms. Fan Tongzhang as recorder. The proceedings were formal, and several important motions were passed. Finally, entertainment was added, with singing and dancing of unparalleled beauty. Here are some gleanings from the event to enrich this account.

The entertainment began, and the first to win applause was Ms. Wang Baomin's Peking opera tune, "Phoenix Hairpin." Ms. Wang is in her blossoming years, with braids over her shoulders. Her voice is melodious, and her demeanor charming and innocent. Her first attempt at singing silenced the clouds. The audience was amazed. It is said that Ms. Wang has studied with famous opera singers, so every time she sings, one feels that "this song should only exist in heaven." She knows many operas. She is graduating from the Department of Sociology this term and is known as a highly talented student.

Next was a comedic dance performed by a man and a woman. Ms. Zhou Changming dressed in men's clothing and a hat, resembling a dashing young man. Ms. Li Suzhen played a country girl. Together, they performed the Charlestown dance, deliberately making mistakes to elicit laughter. They also sang the Fengyang Flower Drum song, making the audience smile. This kind of dance that blends Chinese and foreign elements is fresh and charming, full of interest. Therefore, after the dance, the cries of "one more!" did not cease.

The next act was a speech delivered by a local and a foreigner. Ms. Liang Peishu, the previously dignified and respected chairwoman, played a corrupt old gentleman. Her companion was a comedic local pretending to be foreign, played by Ms. Guo Zhenyl of the Department of Journalism. Ms. Guo gave a speech in a pidgin language, which Ms. Liang translated into Yangzhou dialect. Their expressions and accents were hilarious. Both ladies are fluent in English and Chinese, reaching the height of artistry.

Finally, there was a two-person comic act by Ms. Guo Zhenyl and Ms. Fan Tongzhang. Ms. Guo, originally from Hubei, played a young girl from Hubei, calling herself a candidate. Ms. Fan, a native of Ningbo, played a young lady from Ningbo who had just arrived in the city, speaking with a full Ningbo accent. The audience was in stitches.

There were many other entertainment programs, including the singing and dancing of Ms. Hu Heping, Ms. Ouyang Meide, and others, all of which were excellent. The get-together ended joyfully around ten o'clock. It is said that the association recently initiated the Shanghai Young Women's Aspiration Society and has gained the support of female student associations from various universities. Ms. Guo Zhenyl, Ms. Liang Peishu, Ms. Wang Baomin, and others will represent the society. The International Women's Day celebration on March 8 will be organized by the society. In the future, the society's get-togethers will be even larger in scale.

New Films in Paris 159

— She Yu

Recently, various movie theaters have been competing to screen new films, emerging endlessly, which can be described as a prosperous time. Among them, sound films are particularly abundant in supply. Unfortunately, most focus on divinity and idealism, and there are not many exciting plot-driven films. The Paris Cinema on Hualong Road has always been known for its carefully selected silent films. With its excellent location and affordable ticket prices, its business has flourished, surpassing previous records. A month ago, the manager of the cinema, Mr. Han, said that sound films would be screened. Yesterday, the press was invited to attend a trial screening of "A Woman's Diversion," the sound film he had chosen. The film stars a famous Russian actress. The plot revolves around a coachman who is seduced by a noblewoman, causing his perfect family to break apart. His son dies, and his wife flees. When he seeks solace from the noblewoman, she rejects him coldly, only regarding him as a temporary diversion, not true love. He is also ridiculed by many. The acting is deeply insightful and extremely thorough. The depiction of the social classes and their various situations is also exceptionally powerful. I believe that after watching this film, the audience will understand that the title of the film contains a significant warning.

Travels in India 160

— Linghua

On November 13th, at 3 PM, I boarded a ship to Calcutta, India, at the Latt Pier. Wang Fangyuan brought his child to see me off and took care of everything. Chen Yitong left on the same day for Penang. I was supposed to sit in the third-class cabin due to the tropical heat and bought a ticket for sixteen yuan. The ship departed from Yangon at 5 PM, heading east initially, then turning south into the Bay of Bengal, sailing west towards India.

November 14th. The seawater in the distance appeared black, like the black sea of the Bohai Sea. I felt very comfortable on the ship. There was no wind. The ship was filled with Indians, with only three or four Chinese. There was a Cantonese woman who lived in India and an antique merchant who traded in Calcutta. In the tropics, people generally drink raw water, and I am used to it. It is very suitable and can also be used for showering. A large ship is better than a small steamer. There are many vendors selling various foods on the ship. Eating Indian food costs four annas a meal, which is very cheap. I observed the clothing issue of the Indians and gradually realized that there was no need for elaborate clothing. The Indians had no so-called clothes, just a piece of cloth draped around their bodies. However, they wrapped it in a specific way, like the Guanyin figure in Chinese paintings, which is entirely based on Indian women's clothing. For the Indian people, one piece of cloth is sufficient for clothing. In winter, they add a blanket, which they drape over themselves at night or wear as a robe. It can also be used as formal wear for attending any banquet. For ordinary people, one piece of cloth is sufficient for both day and night. If they want to be clean, two pieces of cloth can be used for washing. Now, most Indians use Gandhi's non-cooperation method, weaving and using their own cloth. All foreign goods are not selling well, so British machines are useless. However, it is also because the Indians originally had no clothing problem, so Gandhi's teachings are easy to implement.

November 16th. At 8 AM, we arrived in Calcutta. My three pieces of luggage were searched very thoroughly, regardless of passports, but checking for writing. The goods were unloaded, and a coolie charged one and a half yuan for a horse-drawn carriage to the Maha Bodhi Society at George Square. This Buddhist society was founded in 1892 by Dharmapala. It has branches in London and New York. The first Buddhist temple is currently being built in Sarnath, along with a university. The Chinese monk Taixu has promised to send ten students. They publish a monthly English newspaper. There is a library and reading room, and many Buddhist books and photos are published. Those who wish to buy them can remit money to the address listed above. The upper floor is a Buddhist hall, with a fascinating depiction of Buddhist history. When entering the hall to worship, one must take off shoes. However, the floor is covered with cement, which is extremely clean and dust-free. The construction costs of this society are 50,000 yuan. It was initially founded thanks to a woman from Honolulu, Mrs. Mirry, who donated 80,000 yuan.

November 17th. I visited Consul Lu Chunfang and Wang Zhiyuan of the party branch. Most of the overseas Chinese here are Cantonese. There is no newspaper yet, but they are working on it. Chinatown is the old lane of Indian Right Time, very dilapidated and narrow. There are extremely poor people, as poor as the poor households in our country. However, the people who come to India seem to have lived here for a long time, even for generations. There is a large Cantonese hotel, with Chen Zhengping as the manager. I saw many Westerners eating there, as well as wealthy Indians coming in pairs, wearing impressive clothes. Gandhi's doctrine is difficult to implement among the wealthy.

The Tides of Gold Market 161

The price of gold rose by six taels yesterday. The price of gold that was benchmarked on March 21st has slightly increased again. The state is still very chaotic and unpredictable. It is a wave of ups and downs. From morning to noon, there were sixteen or seventeen taels of disparity. As for the foreign exchange situation, it seems stable, but the prices are not moving. The overseas silver market seems to be trending differently, with England rising and America falling. The gold price should open high. Minor brokers traded smoothly. Many parties increased their holdings, and short sellers also pushed in. Companies like Fuchang, Yuanheng, Chengfeng, Yongxin, Henghengxing, and Yuan were mainly buying, while Yuanmao, Yonghengxing, and Yuantai were mainly selling. Later, the market price once fell within six hundred and ninety taels, as the exchange bills were insufficient and sales came from the Guangdong group. Coupled with the excitement of buyers and the arbitrage of English gold within the industry, the bank selling price was only calculated at three pence eight seven five. This led to a surge of wind and waves, frequently moving forward, surging more than ten taels and suddenly exceeding seven hundred taels. However, the situation was fleeting, and people were at a loss. Finally, there was a latent softening trend in the afternoon due to the Saturday market closure. Looking back to last week, the market atmosphere was extremely chaotic. It coincided with the swap period, and in these six days of May, there were more than fifty-one taels of twists and turns. On this swap date (16th), the first session rose by thirteen taels.

The situation in the yarn and flower market is unfolding 165

The yarn market was tired in the morning and rose in the afternoon, but the trend is still tight, because the surrounding environment is good and the actual needs are developing daily. The period is in the spring sales, and the Chinese yarn output to foreign countries is still good. Because the Dongyang yarn price is high, the local yarn is cheaper, so the purchase is endless. Therefore, the Southern Ocean Bank is searching for Japanese yarn in the market quite smoothly. It is heard that the Sichuan gang is negotiating between the two sides due to water feet problems, or a large number of transactions will be concluded. However, the general retail investors are doing their best to sell off their thick bottoms, and they will come out as soon as they rise slightly. However, according to the actual situation, this year's situation is better than this time last year. First, the Japanese yarn price last year was low and came to China, but now it is the opposite. Secondly, the domestic situation is quieter and the raw materials are expensive. There are these two major reasons, and a certain giant merchant's bullish attitude is tough. However, the current demand is too stagnant, so it is not perfect.

The early morning of the artificial label was soft and the afternoon was strong. The pre-market of the artificial label opened with the American cotton fatigue, and the market fell slightly. The cotton market is slightly weakened by the influence of dull foreign cotton. However, due to the scarcity of bottom goods, new short sellers do not take reckless actions, so transactions are particularly calm and the volume of transactions is quite small.

Last Week's Rebound in American Cotton 168

A telegram from New York on the 20th reports on the cotton market during the week. The cotton market was strong last week, rebounding about half of the previous week's decline, due to buying by the industry and short covering, and also due to reduced supply when prices fell. When the May price reached above 11 cents, the supply slightly increased, but spot goods in the South were reportedly still being held firmly. Currently, people in the industry all regard the arrangement of new cotton as the principle of revitalization, and even use the stock market situation as a barometer of the market. Private reports indicate that the reduction in cotton fields is between 30% and 20%. The textile market lacks activity, and speculators are also waiting for the development of new cotton and the attitude of the Agricultural Administration Bureau. Flour Market Steps Downward 172

Yesterday, after the opening of the flour market in the morning, the market for each month was quite stable at the beginning of the current month. However, the opening price of the forward saw a sharp contraction. Although the price of foreign wheat did not rise or fall much, and the gold market also saw a slight turnaround, the current trend seemed to have shifted to reality, and there was little relationship with the exchange rate. Because the chips set were all real, the short position felt unusually stable. This was a fact recognized by all parties. The decline in the morning was driven by foreign flour, because the telegram of 2.7 yuan for Flag Flour had been transferred. Brokers such as Zhao had already finalized 20,000 bags, so people's hearts were very empty and unanimously moved downward. In the afternoon, for this reason, factories continued to sell off greatly, so they all fell wearily. It seemed that foreign wheat stopped dumping, and foreign flour was revived. In this situation where one wave was not yet settled and another wave rose again, the bleak future can be foreseen. The June, July, and August months all broke through the 2 liang mark, and the near term also fell sharply at the same time. As a result, March and April fell sharply by 3 fen and 2.5 li, May fell by 3.5 fen, and June fell by 2 fen and 7 li, and July and August fell by 3 fen.

Wheat Prices Fall Sharply 173

Yesterday, after the opening of the futures wheat market in the morning and afternoon, the market for each month saw a state of decline. Because the current month was approaching delivery, although the receiving party was also around 100 cars, the deliverers were between 200 cars. The long and short sides were balanced, and there seemed to be a surplus. Therefore, floating longs and speculators could no longer resist and closed their positions one after another. The future months became more and more deserted because it was rumored that foreign flour had opened up again, and the need for wheat in the future became more and more cold. And the weather was unusually good and bad. In a flash, the new wheat had a considerable relationship, so the selling was strong and the fall was very large. As a result, the current month fell by 7 fen from the previous day, April fell by 4 fen, May fell by 5 fen, and June, July, and August fell by 4 fen.
